<!----><!---->                  <div class="feed-shared-update-v2__description-wrapper" style="" tabindex="-1">
<div class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text
    feed-shared-update-v2__description feed-shared-inline-show-more-text--minimal-padding
    
    
    
    " tabindex="-1">
          <div class="update-components-text relative feed-shared-update-v2__commentary " dir="ltr">
<!---->
  <span class="break-words">
<!---->      <span><span dir="ltr">Worst Experience with GCP Vertex AI:<br>I hade been setting up a project that uses OpenAI's API to generate embeddings on a data and store it in vector DB like Pinecone, FAISS, Google Match Engine. I choose Match Engine due to requirements from my client as the Vector DB. Little did I know that setting up Vector Index on Match Engine is so cumbersome as it requires you to setup a VPC, Peer it with Match Service, Create Endpoint on the Network, Deploy Index. Also all above steps should be done in same region. This is cumbersome then using Pinecone, FAISS etc but doable.<br><br> Now for the query part they have mentioned in their sample notebook: That to query on index you need to create a new notebook that is on the network and region that you made index on such that request is generated from same network. Again a bit cumbersome but not the worse experience.<br><br>After doing all above steps I still was getting connection timed out which they mentioned can happen if network/region of notebook does not match of index. After 4 days of straight debugging I tried to use google cloud run (A service that allows to run code and expose an API in a app like environment) service thinking that notebook might not be running in same network/region and cloud run should run in it. Voila it worked. After going through the docs a bit more I found this:<br>"Requests to your notebook from the JupyterLab interface may be routed through a different region than selected above depending on service availability."<br><br>Summary: Google requires you to make a notebook in the same region as index to query index, but depending on availability it might be routed through another region making it impossible to use their service the way it is intended to use it.<br><br>Reference clause that tells NB to be created in same regions: <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=googlecloud&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A7044797093583986688" data-attribute-index="0">#googlecloud</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=gcp&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A7044797093583986688" data-attribute-index="1">#gcp</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=vertexai&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A7044797093583986688" data-attribute-index="2">#vertexai</a>  </span></span>
  </span>
</div>
<button role="button" class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text__see-more-less-toggle see-more t-14 t-black--light t-normal hoverable-link-text" aria-label="see more, visually reveals content which is already detected by screen readers" type="button">
      <span class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text__see-more-text">…see more</span>
    </button><!----></div>

      <a tabindex="-1" href="/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6950411796960706560/" id="ember977" class="tap-target update-components-mini-update-v2__link-to-details-page text-body-medium ember-view">
<div class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text
    feed-shared-update-v2__description feed-shared-inline-show-more-text--minimal-padding

            <div class="update-components-text relative feed-shared-update-v2__commentary " dir="ltr">
<!---->
  <span class="break-words">
<!---->      <span><span dir="ltr">After using GCP BigQuery, AWS Redshift, Alibaba Cloud Data Studio and few other data warehousing platforms, my personal opinion is that Alibaba Cloud Data Studio is the best among all in terms of service offerings and user experience.<br><br>Why? Everything data related is integrated into a single solution i.e. Data Studio.<br><br>- You can write HiveQL, Python, Spark, Bash or even core MapReduce in Java querying the same tables maintained in MaxCompute.<br>- Automatic DAG Management. You write your code, the platform will take care of dependencies.<br>- Detailed logging for all jobs with query execution plans, queues and resource consumption.<br>- One click Kafka streams to ingest data on near real time basis.<br>- Automated schema mapping from any relational database source. <br>- Support to ingest NoSQL data sources using basic configuration on DataX.<br>- Easy and automated data governance. For example, automatically finds user phone number and protects them in MaxCompute tables.<br>- Direct integration with Alibaba BI tool where dashboards can be created with an intuitive UI and reload can be scheduled as downstream of the ETL DAG.<br>- Automatically maintained data catalog, metadata and table/column lineage.<br>- Direct integration with business maintained dimension tables.<br>- UI based Machine Learning tools.<br>- Automated data quality checks.<br>- Automated alerts and resource monitoring.<br>- Automated code versioning, code library, code sharing and deployment.<br>- Templating snippets in code.<br>- Direct integration with messaging tool called DingTalk to send alerts, reports or dashboard screenshots.<br><br>All the open source Apache big data components have been combined under a single roof.<br><br>The only two drawbacks are: <br>1. Lacks support of open source tools and third party apps. Even loading a basic Python library becomes a pain.<br>2. Network issues in interacting with data residing outside China.<br><br>Alibaba Cloud Data Studio seems one step ahead of the modern data stack! <br><br>Please enlighten me with any better data warehousing platforms that I haven't worked on yet. Snowflake, DataBricks, Talend or anything that offers more? Let's discuss in comments!<br><br><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=data&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="0">#data</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=machinelearning&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="1">#machinelearning</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=python&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="2">#python</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=aws&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="3">#aws</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=cloud&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="4">#cloud</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=dataengineering&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="5">#dataengineering</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=datawarehouse&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6950769642537676800" data-attribute-index="6">#datawarehouse</a> </span></span>
  </span>
</div>

<!---->
  <span class="break-words">
<!---->      <span><span dir="ltr">Google's new text-to-image generation model is really mind-blowing. These sample generations are so far above what we thought was possible just 2 years ago!<br><br>From "Photorealistic Text-to-Image Diffusion Models with Deep Language Understanding"<br><br>Project page: <a href="https://lnkd.in/eiCWtpqd" data-attribute-index="0">https://lnkd.in/eiCWtpqd</a><br><br>But also: "We train on a combination of internal datasets" is becoming de facto only shared details on training data in text-to-image research.<br><br>This is not a good direction for a field that wants to be scientific.<br><br>There is a large spectrum of things we could do to improve this  (I'm talking about research work here, not product advertisements):<br>- give more statistics/measurements on datasets instead of giving only there size<br>- give more pre-training data ablations and strive to better disentangle model and data contributions to performance improvements<br>- help build and share better public datasets if they are essential to performance improvements<br>- ...<br><br>Let's build more reproducible and trustful research. We are lucky to be able to do this in computer science versus other research fields in which reproducibility can be so much more difficult (physics, biology).</span></span>
  </span>
</div>
<button role="button" class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text__see-more-less-toggle see-more t-14 t-black--light t-normal hoverable-link-text" aria-label="see more, visually reveals content which is already detected by screen readers" type="button">

      <a tabindex="-1" href="/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6929867824987324416/" id="ember824" class="tap-target update-components-mini-update-v2__link-to-details-page text-body-medium ember-view">

            <div class="update-components-text relative feed-shared-update-v2__commentary " dir="ltr">
<!---->
  <span class="break-words">
<!---->      <span><span dir="ltr">Why data scientists are leaving their jobs? <br><br>Because they found that they are doing "data science engineering" instead of "data science research":<br>• Most companies have mature A/B testing tools, and data scientists design metrics and automate business reports (BI Engineering).<br>• For machine learning, it's easy to load a model from sklearn, and a lot of work is actually in feature engineering and putting models in production.<br>• When you don't have data, you need to do data engineering to build data pipelines.<br><br>This reality is different from their expectation.<br><br>But a data scientist's job is to provide business value, all the above engineering work is key in solving the business problems, and those work also requires knowledge in statistics and algorithms.<br><br>Does it mean we just give up our research interest? No. <br>So how do we balance the two?<br><br>• talk to your manager to work on a side project for your interest<br>• lead a knowledge sharing or paper reading group<br>• co-author papers with your team <br><br>To have a fulfilling career as a data scientist, you need to balance creating values for your team and nourishing your own passion.<br><br>Otherwise you'll either underperform or burn out. <br><br>While your key responsibilities are defined by your company,  YOU can define your own scope. Don't be afraid to initiate projects that didn't exist.<br><br>You have the power to define your own path.<br><br>*I share more on data science and career on <a href="http://www.dalianaliu.com" data-attribute-index="1">www.dalianaliu.com</a>, free to subscribe.<br><br><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=datascience&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6931978779867164672" data-attribute-index="0">#datascience</a></span></span>
  </span>
</div>
<button role="button" class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text__see-more-less-toggle see-more t-14 t-black--light t-normal hoverable-link-text" aria-label="see more, visually reveals content which is already detected by screen readers" type="button">
      <span class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text__see-more-text">…see more</span>
    </button><!----></div>      </a>

  <span class="break-words">
<!---->      <span><span dir="ltr">With the goal in my mind to make the web more accessible, I have designed a concept of an app Audle. It will help people with disabilities such as down syndrome and cerebral palsy to search through any video streaming platform through their voice command with special word matching ability. <br><br>I have shared the first draft of mockups here and will soon be sharing a mid-fidelity prototype, video explanation, and a case study for the process of designing Audle.<br><br>I am looking forward to getting feedback from seniors in the industry to make this concept more accessible and user-friendly.<br><br><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=accessibility&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6909113914299486208" data-attribute-index="0">#accessibility</a> <a       <a tabindex="-1" href="/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6870751033220505600/" id="ember316" class="tap-target update-components-mini-update-v2__link-to-details-page text-body-medium ember-view">
<div class="feed-shared-inline-show-more-text
    feed-shared-update-v2__description feed-shared-inline-show-more-text--minimal-padding
    
    
    
    " tabindex="-1">
            <div class="update-components-text relative feed-shared-update-v2__commentary " dir="ltr">
<!---->
  <span class="break-words">
<!---->      <span><span dir="ltr">Dear <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=datascientists&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="0">#datascientists</a>, now, as my post about the logistic regression ( <a href="https://lnkd.in/ednkCbHw" data-attribute-index="17">https://lnkd.in/ednkCbHw</a> ) is slowly fading away from your feeds, let's check the level of understanding why the "logistic regression is a regression" (of course can be applied for classification, if you defined the threshold for the predicted probability).<br><br>For those, who didn't read my post - it's written against the rising level of nonsensical tutorials claiming wrongly that "logistic regression is not regression" (google for it).<br><br>In the meantime, let me recall:<br><br>- regression is *never* about the raw DV (response) - which can be of any type, either numeric or categoric - but always about a conditional statistics of it - which is always numeric. Typically the statistics is the expected value (mean) but can be also a quartile or trimmed mean<br><br>- regression, can be used for:<br>a) assessments of the magnitude, standard error and statistical significance of model coefficients to see the way each affects the response<br><br>/Some use it in so-called "stepwise methods of variable selection", but just google for "why we hate stepwise regression" and forget it/<br><br>b) assessment of the marginal and interaction effects - if you subject the regression model to the analysis of deviance<br><br>/ ANOVA is a special case of the "Analysis of Deviance", and it's based on the general linear model. Analysis of Deviance isn't limited to any kind of a regression model and doesn't require any assumptions. In R it's called via car::Anova or stats::anova and can be applied to dozens of models, including quantile or Cox regression/<br><br>c) extrapolation, including prediction of future values. This is a 2-step action: first you calculate the regression model, then you provide the range of new data to make the prediction based on that.<br><br>/ this is where you use it for the classification: 1) you build a logistic regression model based on the training data, 2) then you use it to predict the probability of a success (that's the E(Y|X) - recall the binomial distribution to get it) per given values of the predictor, 3) you apply a decision rule to the predicted probability and obtain the final class /<br><br>- logistic regression is no different (in terms of the "engine" for estimating the model coefficients) from any other special case of the Generalized Linear Model (with small extensions), like linear/Poisson/negative binomial/beta (VGLM)/gamma/ordinal LR &amp; multinomial.<br><br>- logistic regression was invented in the end of 19th century for regression techniques, long before the common framework of the GLM (detains in the post I linked above)<br><br>In the next year I will initiate a website "logistic_regression_is_regression dotcom", by the way.<br><br><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=statistics&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="1">#statistics</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=machinelearning&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="2">#machinelearning</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=logisticregression&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="3">#logisticregression</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=classification&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="4">#classification</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=regression&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="5">#regression</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=datascience&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="6">#datascience</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=dataanalytics&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="7">#dataanalytics</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=dataanalysis&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="8">#dataanalysis</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=ml&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="9">#ml</a> <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=ai&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="10">#ai</a> <a <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/feed/hashtag/?keywords=automl&amp;highlightedUpdateUrns=urn%3Ali%3Aactivity%3A6871181439145177088" data-attribute-index="12">#automl</a> <a
